						<!-- firstHeading -->
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Solar System</h1>
			<!-- /firstHeading -->
			<!-- bodyContent -->
			<div id="bodyContent">
				<!-- tagline -->
				<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
				<!-- /tagline -->
				<!-- subtitle -->
				<div id="contentSub">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Solar_system&amp;redirect=no" title="Solar system">Solar system</a>)</div>
				<!-- /subtitle -->
																<!-- jumpto -->
				<div id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to: <a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>,
					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<!-- /jumpto -->
								<!-- bodytext -->
				<div class="metadata topicon" id="protected-icon" style="display:none; right:55px;"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi" title="This article is semi-protected."><img alt="Page semi-protected" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Padlock-silver-medium.svg/20px-Padlock-silver-medium.svg.png" width="20" height="20" /></a></div>
<div class="dablink">This article is about the Sun and its planetary system. For other systems, see <a href="/wiki/Planetary_system" title="Planetary system">planetary system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star_system" title="Star system">star system</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Planets2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Planets2008.jpg/390px-Planets2008.jpg" width="390" height="219" class="thumbimage" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Planets2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="http://bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">Planets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planets</a> of the Solar System. Sizes are to scale, but relative distances from the Sun are not.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>Solar System</b><sup class="reference" id="ref_Anone"><a href="#endnote_Anone">[a]</a></sup> consists of the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> and those <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_objects" title="Astronomical objects" class="mw-redirect">astronomical objects</a> bound to it by <a href="/wiki/Gravitation" title="Gravitation">gravity</a>, all of which were formed from the collapse of a giant <a href="/wiki/Molecular_cloud" title="Molecular cloud">molecular cloud</a> approximately 4.6 billion years ago. Of the many objects that <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> the Sun, most of the <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a> is contained within eight relatively solitary <a href="/wiki/Planets" title="Planets" class="mw-redirect">planets</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_Enone"><a href="#endnote_Enone">[e]</a></sup> whose orbits are almost circular and lie within a nearly flat disc called the <a href="/wiki/Plane_of_the_ecliptic" title="Plane of the ecliptic">ecliptic plane</a>. The four smaller inner planets, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, also called the <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_planets" title="Terrestrial planets" class="mw-redirect">terrestrial planets</a>, are primarily composed of rock and metal. The four outer planets, the <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">gas giants</a>, are substantially more massive than the terrestrials. The two largest, <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>, are composed mainly of hydrogen and helium; the two outermost planets, <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a>, are composed largely of <a href="/wiki/Volatiles" title="Volatiles">ices</a>, such as water, ammonia and methane, and are often referred to separately as "ice giants".</p>
<p>The Solar System is also home to two regions populated by smaller objects. The <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>, which lies between Mars and Jupiter, is similar to the terrestrial planets as it is composed mainly of rock and metal. Beyond Neptune's orbit lie <a href="/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object" title="Trans-Neptunian object">trans-Neptunian objects</a> composed mostly of ices such as water, ammonia and methane. Within these two regions, five individual objects, <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haumea_(dwarf_planet)" title="Haumea (dwarf planet)">Haumea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Makemake_(dwarf_planet)" title="Makemake (dwarf planet)">Makemake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">Eris</a>, are recognized to be large enough to have been rounded by their own gravity, and are thus termed <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planets" title="Dwarf planets" class="mw-redirect">dwarf planets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="ref_Enone"><a href="#endnote_Enone">[e]</a></sup> In addition to thousands of <a href="/wiki/Small_Solar_System_body" title="Small Solar System body">small bodies</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_Enone"><a href="#endnote_Enone">[e]</a></sup> in those two regions, various other small body populations, such as <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">comets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centaur_(minor_planet)" title="Centaur (minor planet)">centaurs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_dust" title="Interplanetary dust" class="mw-redirect">interplanetary dust</a>, freely travel between regions.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">solar wind</a>, a flow of <a href="/wiki/Plasma_(physics)" title="Plasma (physics)">plasma</a> from the Sun, creates a <a href="/wiki/Stellar_wind_bubble" title="Stellar wind bubble">bubble</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">interstellar medium</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Heliosphere" title="Heliosphere">heliosphere</a>, which extends out to the edge of the scattered disc. The hypothetical <a href="/wiki/Oort_cloud" title="Oort cloud">Oort cloud</a>, which acts as the source for <a href="/wiki/Long-period_comet" title="Long-period comet" class="mw-redirect">long-period comets</a>, may also exist at a distance roughly a thousand times further than the heliosphere.</p>
<p>Six of the <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planets</a> and three of the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planets</a> are orbited by <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">natural satellites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="ref_Bnone"><a href="#endnote_Bnone">[b]</a></sup> usually termed "moons" after Earth's <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>. Each of the outer planets is encircled by <a href="/wiki/Planetary_ring" title="Planetary ring">planetary rings</a> of dust and other particles.</p>
